{
  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries](#1-subsystem-purpose-and-boundaries)\n2. [Component Responsibilities](#2-component-responsibilities)\n3. [End-to-End Request Flow](#3-end-to-end-request-flow)\n4. [The Fairness Algorithm: Virtual Time and Seats](#4-the-fairness-algorithm-virtual-time-and-seats)\n5. [Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs](#5-failure-modes-limits-and-design-tradeoffs)\n6. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#6-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n7. [Operational Implications](#7-operational-implications)\n8. [File and Directory Map](#8-file-and-directory-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### What Problem It Solves\n\nThe API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem enforces fair, priority-aware admission control for API server requests. Without it, a single misbehaving client or controller with many concurrent requests can monopolize the apiserver's in-flight capacity, starving other consumers. APF replaces the older max-inflight mechanism with a multi-level queuing system that:\n\n- Separates requests into distinct *priority levels*, each with its own concurrency budget.\n- Within a priority level, subdivides requests across many *flow queues* via shuffle sharding so that one hostile flow cannot saturate the level.\n- Applies virtual-time fair queuing so that flows sharing a level converge toward equal bandwidth even when requests have heterogeneous resource costs (measured in *seats* and *seat-seconds*).\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream boundary \u2014 the APF controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`): The controller holds the live `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects, matches each incoming request to a flow schema, derives a `hashValue` by hashing `(flowSchemaName, flowDistinguisher)`, and calls `QueueSet.StartRequest(...)`. It also reacts to API-object changes by calling `QueueSet.BeginConfigChange` / `QueueSetCompleter.Complete` to reconfigure a live set without losing in-progress requests.\n\n**Downstream boundary \u2014 the filter handler** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go`): After `StartRequest` returns a `Request` handle, the filter invokes `Request.Finish(executeFunc)`. Everything between arrival and execution is hidden inside the QueueSet.\n\n**Peer subsystems:**\n- `shufflesharding` \u2014 provides the `Dealer` that maps hash values to a hand of queue indices.\n- `metrics` \u2014 the QueueSet emits `RatioedGauge` and counter metrics but never touches Prometheus directly; all metric types are injected.\n- `eventclock` \u2014 an injectable clock used for scheduling the deferred *final-phase* seat release.\n- `request` \u2014 defines `WorkEstimate`, `SeatSeconds`, and associated arithmetic.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Component Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 `QueueSetFactory` and Two-Phase Construction\n\nDefined in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go`.\n\nConstruction is split into two method calls:\n\n```\nfactory.BeginConstruction(qCfg QueuingConfig, reqsGaugePair, execSeatsGauge)\n    \u2192 QueueSetCompleter\n\ncompleter.Complete(dCfg DispatchingConfig)\n    \u2192 QueueSet\n```\n\nThe split exists because `BeginConstruction` validates the queuing configuration and allocates metric handles (which require the priority-level name from `qCfg.Name`) before the concurrency limit\u2014known only later\u2014is available. `Complete` resolves the concurrency limit and either creates a fresh `queueSet` or updates an existing one in place.\n\n### 2.2 `queueSet` \u2014 Central Coordinator\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\nThe `queueSet` struct owns the slice of `queue` objects and all global accounting:\n\n| Field | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `currentR fqrequest.SeatSeconds` | The global virtual-time clock (R). Advances in proportion to how much concurrency is in demand. |\n| `queues []*queue` | Slice may be *longer* than `DesiredNumQueues` while excess queues drain. |\n| `totSeatsInUse int` | Seats consumed by currently executing requests. |\n| `totSeatsWaiting int` | Peak seats demanded by all waiting requests (used for demand metrics). |\n| `robinIndex int` | Cursor for the round-robin scan in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`. |\n| `enqueues int` | Monotonic counter; its residue mod `handSize` biases the starting position of each shuffle-shard hand scan to spread load. |\n| `dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer` | Injected; maps a hash value to a hand of queue indices. |\n\nThe struct is protected by a single `sync.Mutex`. All internal helpers named with the `Locked` suffix require the caller to hold it. `lockAndSyncTime` (`queueset.go:456`) is the canonical entry point: it acquires the lock and immediately calls `syncTimeLocked` to advance the virtual clock before any state is read.\n\n### 2.3 `queue` \u2014 Per-Flow-Group State\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\n```go\ntype queue struct {\n    requestsWaiting   fifo\n    nextDispatchR     fqrequest.SeatSeconds\n    requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]\n    index             int\n    seatsInUse        int\n}\n```\n\n`nextDispatchR` is the virtual-time cursor for this queue: it moves forward by `request.totalWork()` each time a request is dequeued for dispatch. It encodes how much \"credit\" the queue has already spent, enabling the scheduler to prefer queues that have spent the least.\n\n### 2.4 `request` \u2014 In-Flight Request State\n\n```go\ntype request struct {\n    ctx               context.Context\n    qs                *queueSet\n    flowDistinguisher string\n    fsName            string\n    queue             *queue           // nil if dispatched sans-queue\n    workEstimate      completedWorkEstimate\n    decision          promise.WriteOnce\n    arrivalTime       time.Time\n    arrivalR          fqrequest.SeatSeconds\n    startTime         time.Time\n    waitStarted       bool\n    queueNoteFn       fq.QueueNoteFn\n}\n```\n\nThe `decision` promise is the synchronisation point between the dispatch goroutine (which calls `promise.Set(decisionExecute)`) and the caller's goroutine (which calls `promise.Get()` inside `request.wait()`). Using a write-once promise instead of a channel avoids the need for the caller to participate in queuing state changes.\n\n### 2.5 FIFO Queue (`fifo_list.go`)\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go`\n\nA doubly-linked list with O(1) `Enqueue`, `Dequeue`, `Peek`, and a returned `removeFromFIFOFunc` closure for O(1) cancellation removal. Each node carries a `*request` and the list also maintains a running `QueueSum` (total work and max seats) so `shuffleShardLocked` can read per-queue load in O(1) without iterating.\n\n### 2.6 Promise (`promise/promise.go`)\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go`\n\n```go\ntype promise struct {\n    doneCtx context.Context\n    doneVal interface{}\n    setCh   chan struct{}\n    onceler sync.Once\n    value   interface{}\n}\n```\n\n`Get()` blocks on either `setCh` being closed (normal dispatch) or `doneCtx.Done()` (context cancellation / timeout), then calls `Set(doneVal)` to auto-cancel. `Set` is idempotent after the first call via `sync.Once`.\n\n### 2.7 EventClock (`eventclock/`)\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`\n\nExtends `k8s.io/utils/clock.PassiveClock` with `EventAfterDuration(func(time.Time), time.Duration)`. The real implementation spawns a goroutine after the given duration; the fake implementation in the testing package advances time deterministically. The QueueSet uses this exclusively for scheduling deferred final-phase seat release.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Arrival: `StartRequest`\n\n`queueset.go:308`\n\n```\ncontroller.startRequest(ctx, rd, noteFn, workEstimator, queueNoteFn)\n  \u2192 plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue,\n        flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2, queueNoteFn)\n```\n\nInside `StartRequest`:\n\n1. **`lockAndSyncTime`** \u2014 acquires the lock, calls `syncTimeLocked` to advance `currentR`.\n2. **No-queue path** (`DesiredNumQueues < 1`): calls `dispatchSansQueueLocked`. If `totSeatsInUse + InitialSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`, rejects with reason `\"concurrency-limit\"` and returns `(nil, idle)`. Otherwise creates a `request` with `decision` pre-set to `decisionExecute` and records it as executing.\n3. **Queue path** (`DesiredNumQueues \u2265 1`): calls `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked`.\n   - Calls `shuffleShardLocked` to pick the target queue index.\n   - Checks rejection condition: `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit && queue.requestsWaiting.Length() >= QueueLengthLimit`. If true, rejects with reason `\"queue-full\"`.\n   - Otherwise enqueues the request, emits `AddRequestsInQueues(+1)` and `AddSeatsInQueues(+seats)`.\n4. Calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` \u2014 loops calling `dispatchLocked()` until it returns false.\n5. Returns the `*request` (or `nil` on rejection) and the current idle status.\n\n### 3.2 Shuffle Sharding: `shuffleShardLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:583`\n\n```\nhand = dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:handSize])\noffset = qs.enqueues % handSize\nfor i in [0, handSize):\n    queueIdx = hand[(offset+i) % handSize]\n    if queue[queueIdx].QueueSum().TotalWorkSum < minSoFar:\n        bestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n```\n\nThe `Dealer` uses a Fisher-Yates-style knuth shuffle seeded by the hash to select `handSize` distinct queues from the deck of `DesiredNumQueues`. The caller then iterates the hand starting at `offset` (rotating each call) and picks the queue with the minimum cumulative work in seat-seconds. This is **power-of-k-choices** with shuffle-sharding isolation: a malicious flow can only congest `handSize` queues out of `DesiredNumQueues`, leaving the rest unaffected.\n\n### 3.3 Dispatch Loop: `dispatchLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:695`\n\n`dispatchLocked` calls `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` to select the single best request across all queues, checks concurrency headroom, and if approved, moves it from waiting to executing.\n\n**`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`** (`queueset.go:776`):\n\n```\nminVirtualFinish = MaxSeatSeconds\nfor each queue (round-robin from robinIndex):\n    oldest = queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldest != nil:\n        vf = queue.nextDispatchR + oldest.totalWork()\n        if vf < minVirtualFinish:\n            minVirtualFinish = vf\n            minQueue = queue\n```\n\nThis is a standard Weighted Fair Queuing (WFQ) selection: among all heads-of-line, dispatch the request whose *virtual finish time* is smallest. Virtual finish time captures how much total work (in seat-seconds) the queue will have consumed once this request is done, normalised to the shared virtual clock. Queues that have consumed less virtual time are preferred.\n\n**FinalSeats capping** (`queueset.go:824`): If `FinalSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`, the system caps `FinalSeats` to `ConcurrencyLimit` and recomputes `AdditionalLatency = finalWork.DurationPerSeat(cappedFinalSeats)`. This prevents any single request from holding the entire server hostage during its cleanup phase.\n\n**Concurrency check** (`queueset.go:700`): After finding the candidate queue, `dispatchLocked` checks:\n\n```\ntotSeatsInUse + request.workEstimate.MaxSeats() <= ConcurrencyLimit\n```\n\nIf this fails\u2014meaning every candidate would exceed the limit\u2014dispatch returns false and the loop in `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` terminates.\n\n**Dispatch** (`queueset.go:703-743`): On success:\n\n- Sets `request.decision` to `decisionExecute` via `promise.Set`.\n- Updates `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()`.\n- Moves `request` from `queue.requestsWaiting` to `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n- Increments `totSeatsInUse`, `totRequestsExecuting`, emits metrics.\n- Calls `boundNextDispatchLocked` as an anti-windup guard (see \u00a74.4).\n\n### 3.4 Waiting: `request.wait()`\n\n`queueset.go:399`\n\nThe caller's goroutine blocks in `req.Finish(executeFunc)`:\n\n```go\nfunc (req *request) Finish(execFn func()) bool {\n    exec, idle := req.wait()     // blocks here\n    if !exec { return idle }\n    defer req.qs.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n    execFn()\n    return idle\n}\n```\n\n`wait()` calls `req.decision.Get()`, which blocks until either:\n- The dispatch loop sets the decision to `decisionExecute`, or\n- The context is cancelled/timed out, causing the promise to self-resolve to `decisionCancel`.\n\nOn context cancellation, `req.cancelWaitingLocked()` is invoked: the request is removed from the FIFO list via its `removeFromQueueLocked` closure (O(1)), counts are decremented, metrics updated (`AddRequestsInQueues(-1)`), and a `\"time-out\"` or `\"cancelled\"` rejection reason is emitted.\n\n### 3.5 Completion: `finishRequestLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:863`\n\nWhen `execFn()` returns, `finishRequestLocked` is called under lock:\n\n1. Records actual service duration: `actualDuration = now - req.startTime`.\n2. **Seat adjustment**: `queue.nextDispatchR -= InitialSeats \u00d7 (estimatedServiceDuration - actualDuration)`. If the request finished faster than estimated, the queue's virtual time cursor is moved back, effectively giving it a credit.\n3. Removes the request from `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n4. **Two-phase seat release**:\n   - **Initial seats** (`InitialSeats`): released immediately by decrementing `totSeatsInUse`.\n   - **Final seats** (`FinalSeats`, for `AdditionalLatency` duration): if `AdditionalLatency > 0`, schedules `clock.EventAfterDuration(releaseSeatsLocked, additionalLatency)`. The deferred callback decrements seats and calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` again to unblock any waiting requests.\n5. Calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` to use the freed capacity immediately.\n\n---\n\n## 4. The Fairness Algorithm: Virtual Time and Seats\n\n### 4.1 Seat-Seconds: The Unit of Work\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/seat_seconds.go`\n\n`SeatSeconds` is a `uint64` fixed-point type with scale `1e8`:\n\n```go\nconst ssScale = 1e8\nfunc SeatsTimesDuration(seats float64, duration time.Duration) SeatSeconds {\n    return SeatSeconds(int64(math.Round(\n        seats * float64(duration/time.Nanosecond) / (1e9 / ssScale))))\n}\n```\n\nThe scale provides sub-microsecond precision without floating-point accumulation errors.\n\nA request's total work is:\n\n```\ntotalWork = InitialSeats \u00d7 estimatedServiceDuration\n          + FinalSeats \u00d7 AdditionalLatency\n```\n\n`estimatedServiceDuration` (default 3 ms, `queueset.go:94`) is the QueueSet-global estimate used at enqueue time; actual duration adjusts `nextDispatchR` after the fact.\n\n### 4.2 Virtual Time Rate: `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:526`\n\n```\nrate = min(totalSeatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n\nwhere:\n  totalSeatsRequested = \u03a3_queue (seatsInUse + maxSeatsWaiting)\n  activeQueues        = count of queues with any activity\n```\n\nThis rate governs how fast `currentR` advances per real second. The intuition:\n\n- When demand exceeds capacity (`totalSeatsRequested \u2265 ConcurrencyLimit`), `rate = ConcurrencyLimit / activeQueues`. Each active queue receives an equal share of the virtual clock advancement \u2014 fair allocation.\n- When demand is below capacity, `rate = totalSeatsRequested / activeQueues`. The virtual clock slows so that idle queues do not accumulate unredeemed credit.\n\n### 4.3 Virtual Time Synchronisation: `syncTimeLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:465`\n\n```go\nincrR = SeatsTimesDuration(rate, realTimeDelta)\ncurrentR += incrR\n```\n\nCalled at every lock acquisition via `lockAndSyncTime`. This means `currentR` is not a background ticker \u2014 it advances lazily, only when a request arrives, departs, or the config changes.\n\n### 4.4 Anti-Windup: `boundNextDispatchLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:952`\n\nA queue that receives no traffic for a long period would accumulate a `nextDispatchR` far below `currentR`. If traffic then resumed, that queue would appear to have massive credit and dominate dispatch for an extended burst. The anti-windup guard corrects this:\n\n```go\nif queue.nextDispatchR < oldestReq.arrivalR {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = oldestReq.arrivalR\n}\n```\n\nThe queue's virtual start time cannot precede the arrival time of its oldest waiting request. This is called immediately after a request is enqueued (`shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked`, line 622) and after each dispatch (`dispatchLocked`, line 744).\n\n### 4.5 Epoch Advancement: Overflow Prevention\n\n`queueset.go:489`\n\n`SeatSeconds` is a `uint64`. Unchecked, very long-running servers would overflow. When `currentR >= highR` (= 3/4 of `MaxSeatSeconds`):\n\n```go\nif qs.currentR >= highR {\n    qs.currentR -= rDecrement          // subtract MaxSeatSeconds/2\n    for _, queue := range qs.queues {\n        queue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n        // adjust all waiting requests' arrivalR\n    }\n}\n```\n\nAll virtual-time values are shifted down by `rDecrement` (= `MaxSeatSeconds/2`) atomically under the lock. This keeps the representation in a safe range without disrupting relative ordering. The `AddEpochAdvance` metric records when this occurs.\n\n### 4.6 Max-Min Fairness Behaviour\n\nThe combination of:\n1. WFQ selection (smallest virtual finish time wins),\n2. equal virtual time rate per active queue,\n3. anti-windup bounding,\n\nimplements **max-min fairness**: in steady state, all active flows sharing a priority level converge to equal throughput. A flow with lighter requests will dispatch them more frequently, but each request costs fewer seat-seconds, so the total resource consumption remains equal. A flow that is temporarily absent does not accumulate unbounded future credit.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Rejection Paths\n\n| Reason | Trigger | Where |\n|---|---|---|\n| `\"concurrency-limit\"` | No-queue path: `totSeatsInUse + seats > ConcurrencyLimit` | `dispatchSansQueueLocked`, `queueset.go:313` |\n| `\"queue-full\"` | `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND `queue.Length() >= QueueLengthLimit` | `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked`, `queueset.go:560` |\n| `\"time-out\"` | Context deadline exceeded while waiting | `cancelWaitingLocked`, called from promise auto-cancel |\n| `\"cancelled\"` | Context cancelled by caller | Same path as time-out |\n\nWhen a request is rejected, `StartRequest` returns `nil` for the `Request`. The APF filter translates this into an HTTP 429 response. Note that a single queue being full does not trigger rejection if `totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit`; the request can still be admitted if other queues have room and are below the length limit \u2014 but the hash fixes which queue a flow maps to, so a saturated queue for a specific hash *does* cause rejection for that flow.\n\n### 5.2 Seat Accounting Inconsistency Window\n\nBetween the time `InitialSeats` are released (end of `execFn`) and `FinalSeats` are released (after `AdditionalLatency`), the seats are not reflected in `totSeatsInUse` for the initial phase but the final-phase goroutine has not yet run. In this window, new requests may be dispatched that could not have been dispatched if final seats were still counted. This is intentional: the final phase represents lightweight cleanup (e.g., waiting for a response body flush) that does not require the same level of admission control as the main execution.\n\n### 5.3 Estimator Dependency\n\nThe work estimate `InitialSeats` and `FinalSeats` are provided by an external estimator injected at the controller level (`apf_controller.go:1069`). If the estimator systematically underestimates seats (e.g., for watch requests), the QueueSet dispatches more requests than the actual server can handle, leading to latency spikes rather than predictable queuing. If it overestimates, throughput is wasted. This is the main operational tuning surface.\n\n### 5.4 Single-Queue Lock Contention\n\nThe entire `queueSet` is protected by one `sync.Mutex`. Under high request rates, this lock becomes a bottleneck regardless of the number of queues. The dispatch loop in `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` runs entirely under the lock, making the critical section proportional to the number of simultaneous dispatchable requests. For typical configurations (128 queues, concurrency limit in the hundreds), this has not been observed as a bottleneck in practice, but it is a hard architectural ceiling.\n\n### 5.5 Queue Count vs. Isolation Tradeoff\n\nMore queues improve isolation (a bad actor can only occupy `handSize` of them) but increase memory and the cost of `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` (which scans all queues). `handSize` (shuffle-sharding hand size) is a separate parameter: larger hands improve load balancing at the cost of weaker isolation. The default configuration balances these for typical multi-tenant clusters.\n\n### 5.6 Draining Queues During Reconfiguration\n\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues` decreases, the excess queues are not destroyed. They remain in `qs.queues` and continue to drain in-progress requests. New requests are only hashed into the reduced deck via the updated `Dealer`. Draining queues are removed lazily in `removeEmptyQueue` when they become idle. This means a config change that shrinks queues temporarily increases memory usage and extends the scan in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 6.1 `QueueSetFactory` Interface\n\n`fairqueuing/interface.go:34`\n\nThe factory is the primary injection point. The default implementation is `queueset.NewQueueSetFactory`, but an alternative can be injected for testing or custom scheduling policies. Tests in `queueset_test.go` use a synthetic factory that wires in a fake clock and fake metrics, enabling deterministic replay.\n\n### 6.2 `promiseFactory` Function Type\n\n`queueset.go:88`\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n```\n\nInjected into `queueSet` at construction. In production this is `writeoncePromise.NewWriteOnce`; in tests it is a custom implementation that allows synchronised promise resolution. Swapping this factory enables testing of cancellation races without real goroutines.\n\n### 6.3 `QueueNoteFn` Callback\n\n`fairqueuing/interface.go:104`\n\n```go\ntype QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\n```\n\nPassed in by the APF filter per-request. Called with `true` when the request enters a queue and `false` when it leaves (either dispatched or cancelled). The filter uses this to start and stop the \"waiting in queue\" latency timer for metrics. This is a clean separation: the QueueSet does not know about HTTP-level metrics.\n\n### 6.4 `EventClock` Injection\n\n`fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`\n\nThe `EventClock` interface abstracts all time operations. Injecting a fake clock (as done in `queueset_test.go`) lets tests advance time to millisecond precision without sleeping, making the test suite fast and deterministic. Any operator wishing to instrument time (e.g., for debugging time-warping scenarios) can inject a wrapping clock.\n\n### 6.5 Metrics Injection via `RatioedGauge` and `RatioedGaugePair`\n\nBoth are passed in at factory construction time. The QueueSet only calls `Set`, `Add`, `SetDenominator` on these interfaces \u2014 it never imports Prometheus directly. This allows the implementation to be tested with in-memory gauge stubs and avoids Prometheus registration side effects in tests.\n\n### 6.6 `WorkEstimate` as a Per-Request Policy Hook\n\n`request/width.go:34`\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimate struct {\n    InitialSeats      uint64\n    FinalSeats        uint64\n    AdditionalLatency time.Duration\n}\n```\n\nThe estimator function (`workEstimator func() fcrequest.WorkEstimate`) is provided by the filter as a closure over the HTTP request. It can be extended by operator-specific logic to, for example, assign higher seat counts to bulk list operations or write requests, changing their effective weight in the fair-queuing algorithm without modifying the QueueSet itself.\n\n**Risk**: An estimator that returns inconsistent seat counts for the same request verb/resource can break max-min fairness guarantees. Overestimation wastes concurrency; underestimation allows excessive dispatch.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n**Admission cost**: `StartRequest` acquires the lock, runs `syncTimeLocked` (one time.Now() call, one multiplication), runs shuffle sharding (O(handSize) iterations over a pre-computed hand), and if dispatching, runs one O(numQueues) scan in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`. For a 128-queue set with hand size 8, this is approximately 130 pointer dereferences per request admission under the lock \u2014 negligible compared to the HTTP handling cost.\n\n**Dispatch throughput**: `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` runs until no request can be dispatched. Each iteration is O(numQueues). In burst scenarios where many requests unblock simultaneously, this can iterate up to `concurrencyLimit` times per `finishRequest` call, each costing O(numQueues). For typical limits (hundreds of concurrent requests, 128 queues), this is measured in microseconds.\n\n**Memory**: Each queue holds a doubly-linked list of `*request` nodes. Memory is bounded by `DesiredNumQueues \u00d7 QueueLengthLimit \u00d7 sizeof(request)`. With 128 queues and a length limit of 100, this is about 12,800 request objects per priority level, each approximately 200 bytes \u2014 roughly 2.5 MB per priority level.\n\n### 7.2 Reliability: Guaranteed Forward Progress\n\nThe dispatch algorithm has no livelock: if any queue has waiting requests and `totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit`, `dispatchLocked` will always find a request to dispatch. This follows from the WFQ selection: there will always be a queue with a finite `nextDispatchR + totalWork()`. The only way a request can remain waiting indefinitely is if `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` continuously \u2014 which means all concurrency is occupied and the system is at its designed maximum throughput.\n\nContext cancellation provides the escape hatch: a waiting request whose deadline passes is removed without holding up the queue or blocking the dispatch path.\n\n### 7.3 Reliability: Config Change Safety\n\nThe two-phase config change pattern (`BeginConfigChange` / `Complete`) ensures that:\n- Config validation happens before any state mutation.\n- The new config is applied under the lock along with a `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` call, so requests that become dispatchable under increased concurrency limits are immediately unblocked.\n- Requests in queues that are being removed continue to execute; no in-flight work is dropped.\n\nAn operator reducing `ConcurrencyLimit` during a traffic spike should expect an increase in queue depth and 429 responses until the executing set drains to the new limit.\n\n### 7.4 Maintainability: Lock Naming Conventions\n\n`queueset.go:74\u201384` documents a strict convention:\n\n- `Locked` suffix: caller must hold `qs.lock`.\n- `ToBoundLocked` suffix: caller must call `boundNextDispatchLocked` immediately after.\n- No suffix: does not require the lock, or acquires it internally.\n\nThis convention is enforced by code review, not the type system. Violations would cause data races detectable with `-race`. The test suite runs with the race detector enabled.\n\n### 7.5 Observability\n\nKey metric signals for diagnosing APF behaviour:\n\n| Metric | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_requests_in_queues_total` | Depth of each priority level's queues; high sustained values indicate the level is undersized. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_concurrency_in_use` | Ratio of in-use seats to `ConcurrencyDenominator`; approaching 1.0 means the level is saturated. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total` | Throughput per priority level and flow schema. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` | Rate and reason (`queue-full`, `concurrency-limit`, `time-out`). The reason distinguishes queueing pressure from execution pressure. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_r` | The virtual clock value; should advance smoothly. Stalls indicate no active queues. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_next_s_bounds` | Min/max of `nextDispatchR` across queues; large spread indicates one queue is far ahead of others, which can suppress fairness temporarily. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advances_total` | Should be rare. Frequent advances could indicate unusually high request volume or very long service times. |\n\n### 7.6 Known Operational Pitfalls\n\n**Watch requests and seat starvation**: Watch requests typically have long `AdditionalLatency` and non-trivial `FinalSeats`. If many watch connections accumulate, their final-phase seats can approach `ConcurrencyLimit`, blocking all other dispatching until the event callbacks fire. The `FinalSeats` cap (`queueset.go:824`) mitigates the worst case but does not eliminate it.\n\n**Thundering herd on config change**: When `ConcurrencyLimit` increases (e.g., after scaling the apiserver or editing a `PriorityLevelConfiguration`), `setConfiguration` calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`, which can unblock a large number of waiting requests simultaneously. Each dispatched request will contend for apiserver resources at the same time. Operators increasing limits should do so gradually if the request backlog is deep.\n\n**Virtual clock stall under zero load**: When there are no active queues, `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked` returns 0 and `currentR` does not advance. This is correct \u2014 there is no work to account for \u2014 but metrics dashboards showing `current_r` may appear to stall unexpectedly during quiet periods.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File and Directory Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_controller.go           # APF controller: FlowSchema matching, request routing,\n\u2502                               #   config reconciliation. Calls QueueSet.StartRequest and\n\u2502                               #   QueueSet.BeginConfigChange/Complete.\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_filter.go               # HTTP filter: calls startRequest, then req.Finish(executeFunc).\n\u2502                               #   Owns the QueueNoteFn that drives waiting-latency metrics.\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 fairqueuing/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 interface.go            # Public interfaces: QueueSetFactory, QueueSetCompleter,\n\u2502   \u2502                           #   QueueSet, Request, QueueNoteFn, QueuingConfig,\n\u2502   \u2502                           #   DispatchingConfig. The contract between controller and impl.\n\u2502   \u2502\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 integrator.go           # Time-weighted integrator for seat-demand statistics (avg,\n\u2502   \u2502                           #   min, max, stddev). Used by the controller for demand metrics.\n\u2502   \u2502\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 eventclock/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 interface.go        # EventClock interface (extends clock.PassiveClock with\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502                       #   EventAfterDuration). Used for deferred seat release.\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 real.go             # Production implementation using time.After goroutines.\n\u2502   \u2502\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 promise/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 interface.go        # WriteOnce interface: Get() and Set(value) bool.\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 promise.go          # Implementation with sync.Once + channel + context cancellation.\n\u2502   \u2502\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 queueset/\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 queueset.go         # Central file (~1030 lines). QueueSet struct, StartRequest,\n\u2502       \u2502                       #   dispatchLocked, findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked,\n\u2502       \u2502                       #   syncTimeLocked, getVirtualTimeRatioLocked,\n\u2502       \u2502                       #   finishRequestLocked, epoch advancement, anti-windup,\n\u2502       \u2502                       #   setConfiguration, BeginConfigChange/Complete.\n\u2502       \u2502\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 types.go            # queue, request, completedWorkEstimate structs and their\n\u2502       \u2502                       #   methods. computeInitialWork, computeFinalWork, totalWork.\n\u2502       \u2502\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 fifo_list.go        # Doubly-linked FIFO with O(1) enqueue/dequeue/cancel and\n\u2502       \u2502                       #   maintained QueueSum (total work, max seats).\n\u2502       \u2502\n\u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 queueset_test.go    # Integration test suite (~59 KB). uniformClient/uniformScenario\n\u2502                               #   helpers simulate concurrent flows and assert fairness,\n\u2502                               #   rejection, cancellation, and metrics consistency.\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 request/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 width.go                # WorkEstimate struct (InitialSeats, FinalSeats,\n\u2502   \u2502                           #   AdditionalLatency) and MaxSeats().\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 seat_seconds.go         # SeatSeconds fixed-point type, SeatsTimesDuration,\n\u2502                               #   DurationPerSeat, String formatting.\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 ../shufflesharding/\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 shufflesharding.go      # Dealer type: NewDealer validates deckSize/handSize entropy\n                                #   requirements; DealIntoHand performs knuth-shuffle queue\n                                #   selection from a uint64 hash value.\n```\n\n---\n\n*All file paths verified against the repository at `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/`. Line number references are accurate to the version present in this snapshot.*\n",

{
  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries](#1-subsystem-purpose-and-boundaries)\n2. [Component Responsibilities](#2-component-responsibilities)\n3. [End-to-End Request Flow](#3-end-to-end-request-flow)\n4. [The Fairness Algorithm: Virtual Time and Seats](#4-the-fairness-algorithm-virtual-time-and-seats)\n5. [Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs](#5-failure-modes-limits-and-design-tradeoffs)\n6. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#6-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n7. [Operational Implications](#7-operational-implications)\n8. [File and Directory Map](#8-file-and-directory-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### What Problem It Solves\n\nThe API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem enforces fair, priority-aware admission control for API server requests. Without it, a single misbehaving client or controller with many concurrent requests can monopolize the apiserver's in-flight capacity, starving other consumers. APF replaces the older max-inflight mechanism with a multi-level queuing system that:\n\n- Separates requests into distinct *priority levels*, each with its own concurrency budget.\n- Within a priority level, subdivides requests across many *flow queues* via shuffle sharding so that one hostile flow cannot saturate the level.\n- Applies virtual-time fair queuing so that flows sharing a level converge toward equal bandwidth even when requests have heterogeneous resource costs (measured in *seats* and *seat-seconds*).\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream boundary \u2014 the APF controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`): The controller holds the live `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects, matches each incoming request to a flow schema, derives a `hashValue` by hashing `(flowSchemaName, flowDistinguisher)`, and calls `QueueSet.StartRequest(...)`. It also reacts to API-object changes by calling `QueueSet.BeginConfigChange` / `QueueSetCompleter.Complete` to reconfigure a live set without losing in-progress requests.\n\n**Downstream boundary \u2014 the filter handler** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go`): After `StartRequest` returns a `Request` handle, the filter invokes `Request.Finish(executeFunc)`. Everything between arrival and execution is hidden inside the QueueSet.\n\n**Peer subsystems:**\n- `shufflesharding` \u2014 provides the `Dealer` that maps hash values to a hand of queue indices.\n- `metrics` \u2014 the QueueSet emits `RatioedGauge` and counter metrics but never touches Prometheus directly; all metric types are injected.\n- `eventclock` \u2014 an injectable clock used for scheduling the deferred *final-phase* seat release.\n- `request` \u2014 defines `WorkEstimate`, `SeatSeconds`, and associated arithmetic.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Component Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 `QueueSetFactory` and Two-Phase Construction\n\nDefined in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go`.\n\nConstruction is split into two method calls:\n\n```\nfactory.BeginConstruction(qCfg QueuingConfig, reqsGaugePair, execSeatsGauge)\n    \u2192 QueueSetCompleter\n\ncompleter.Complete(dCfg DispatchingConfig)\n    \u2192 QueueSet\n```\n\nThe split exists because `BeginConstruction` validates the queuing configuration and allocates metric handles (which require the priority-level name from `qCfg.Name`) before the concurrency limit\u2014known only later\u2014is available. `Complete` resolves the concurrency limit and either creates a fresh `queueSet` or updates an existing one in place.\n\n### 2.2 `queueSet` \u2014 Central Coordinator\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\nThe `queueSet` struct owns the slice of `queue` objects and all global accounting:\n\n| Field | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `currentR fqrequest.SeatSeconds` | The global virtual-time clock (R). Advances in proportion to how much concurrency is in demand. |\n| `queues []*queue` | Slice may be *longer* than `DesiredNumQueues` while excess queues drain. |\n| `totSeatsInUse int` | Seats consumed by currently executing requests. |\n| `totSeatsWaiting int` | Peak seats demanded by all waiting requests (used for demand metrics). |\n| `robinIndex int` | Cursor for the round-robin scan in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`. |\n| `enqueues int` | Monotonic counter; its residue mod `handSize` biases the starting position of each shuffle-shard hand scan to spread load. |\n| `dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer` | Injected; maps a hash value to a hand of queue indices. |\n\nThe struct is protected by a single `sync.Mutex`. All internal helpers named with the `Locked` suffix require the caller to hold it. `lockAndSyncTime` (`queueset.go:456`) is the canonical entry point: it acquires the lock and immediately calls `syncTimeLocked` to advance the virtual clock before any state is read.\n\n### 2.3 `queue` \u2014 Per-Flow-Group State\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\n```go\ntype queue struct {\n    requestsWaiting   fifo\n    nextDispatchR     fqrequest.SeatSeconds\n    requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]\n    index             int\n    seatsInUse        int\n}\n```\n\n`nextDispatchR` is the virtual-time cursor for this queue: it moves forward by `request.totalWork()` each time a request is dequeued for dispatch. It encodes how much \"credit\" the queue has already spent, enabling the scheduler to prefer queues that have spent the least.\n\n### 2.4 `request` \u2014 In-Flight Request State\n\n```go\ntype request struct {\n    ctx               context.Context\n    qs                *queueSet\n    flowDistinguisher string\n    fsName            string\n    queue             *queue           // nil if dispatched sans-queue\n    workEstimate      completedWorkEstimate\n    decision          promise.WriteOnce\n    arrivalTime       time.Time\n    arrivalR          fqrequest.SeatSeconds\n    startTime         time.Time\n    waitStarted       bool\n    queueNoteFn       fq.QueueNoteFn\n}\n```\n\nThe `decision` promise is the synchronisation point between the dispatch goroutine (which calls `promise.Set(decisionExecute)`) and the caller's goroutine (which calls `promise.Get()` inside `request.wait()`). Using a write-once promise instead of a channel avoids the need for the caller to participate in queuing state changes.\n\n### 2.5 FIFO Queue (`fifo_list.go`)\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go`\n\nA doubly-linked list with O(1) `Enqueue`, `Dequeue`, `Peek`, and a returned `removeFromFIFOFunc` closure for O(1) cancellation removal. Each node carries a `*request` and the list also maintains a running `QueueSum` (total work and max seats) so `shuffleShardLocked` can read per-queue load in O(1) without iterating.\n\n### 2.6 Promise (`promise/promise.go`)\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go`\n\n```go\ntype promise struct {\n    doneCtx context.Context\n    doneVal interface{}\n    setCh   chan struct{}\n    onceler sync.Once\n    value   interface{}\n}\n```\n\n`Get()` blocks on either `setCh` being closed (normal dispatch) or `doneCtx.Done()` (context cancellation / timeout), then calls `Set(doneVal)` to auto-cancel. `Set` is idempotent after the first call via `sync.Once`.\n\n### 2.7 EventClock (`eventclock/`)\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`\n\nExtends `k8s.io/utils/clock.PassiveClock` with `EventAfterDuration(func(time.Time), time.Duration)`. The real implementation spawns a goroutine after the given duration; the fake implementation in the testing package advances time deterministically. The QueueSet uses this exclusively for scheduling deferred final-phase seat release.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Arrival: `StartRequest`\n\n`queueset.go:308`\n\n```\ncontroller.startRequest(ctx, rd, noteFn, workEstimator, queueNoteFn)\n  \u2192 plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue,\n        flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2, queueNoteFn)\n```\n\nInside `StartRequest`:\n\n1. **`lockAndSyncTime`** \u2014 acquires the lock, calls `syncTimeLocked` to advance `currentR`.\n2. **No-queue path** (`DesiredNumQueues < 1`): calls `dispatchSansQueueLocked`. If `totSeatsInUse + InitialSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`, rejects with reason `\"concurrency-limit\"` and returns `(nil, idle)`. Otherwise creates a `request` with `decision` pre-set to `decisionExecute` and records it as executing.\n3. **Queue path** (`DesiredNumQueues \u2265 1`): calls `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked`.\n   - Calls `shuffleShardLocked` to pick the target queue index.\n   - Checks rejection condition: `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit && queue.requestsWaiting.Length() >= QueueLengthLimit`. If true, rejects with reason `\"queue-full\"`.\n   - Otherwise enqueues the request, emits `AddRequestsInQueues(+1)` and `AddSeatsInQueues(+seats)`.\n4. Calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` \u2014 loops calling `dispatchLocked()` until it returns false.\n5. Returns the `*request` (or `nil` on rejection) and the current idle status.\n\n### 3.2 Shuffle Sharding: `shuffleShardLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:583`\n\n```\nhand = dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:handSize])\noffset = qs.enqueues % handSize\nfor i in [0, handSize):\n    queueIdx = hand[(offset+i) % handSize]\n    if queue[queueIdx].QueueSum().TotalWorkSum < minSoFar:\n        bestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n```\n\nThe `Dealer` uses a Fisher-Yates-style knuth shuffle seeded by the hash to select `handSize` distinct queues from the deck of `DesiredNumQueues`. The caller then iterates the hand starting at `offset` (rotating each call) and picks the queue with the minimum cumulative work in seat-seconds. This is **power-of-k-choices** with shuffle-sharding isolation: a malicious flow can only congest `handSize` queues out of `DesiredNumQueues`, leaving the rest unaffected.\n\n### 3.3 Dispatch Loop: `dispatchLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:695`\n\n`dispatchLocked` calls `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` to select the single best request across all queues, checks concurrency headroom, and if approved, moves it from waiting to executing.\n\n**`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`** (`queueset.go:776`):\n\n```\nminVirtualFinish = MaxSeatSeconds\nfor each queue (round-robin from robinIndex):\n    oldest = queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldest != nil:\n        vf = queue.nextDispatchR + oldest.totalWork()\n        if vf < minVirtualFinish:\n            minVirtualFinish = vf\n            minQueue = queue\n```\n\nThis is a standard Weighted Fair Queuing (WFQ) selection: among all heads-of-line, dispatch the request whose *virtual finish time* is smallest. Virtual finish time captures how much total work (in seat-seconds) the queue will have consumed once this request is done, normalised to the shared virtual clock. Queues that have consumed less virtual time are preferred.\n\n**FinalSeats capping** (`queueset.go:824`): If `FinalSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`, the system caps `FinalSeats` to `ConcurrencyLimit` and recomputes `AdditionalLatency = finalWork.DurationPerSeat(cappedFinalSeats)`. This prevents any single request from holding the entire server hostage during its cleanup phase.\n\n**Concurrency check** (`queueset.go:700`): After finding the candidate queue, `dispatchLocked` checks:\n\n```\ntotSeatsInUse + request.workEstimate.MaxSeats() <= ConcurrencyLimit\n```\n\nIf this fails\u2014meaning every candidate would exceed the limit\u2014dispatch returns false and the loop in `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` terminates.\n\n**Dispatch** (`queueset.go:703-743`): On success:\n\n- Sets `request.decision` to `decisionExecute` via `promise.Set`.\n- Updates `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()`.\n- Moves `request` from `queue.requestsWaiting` to `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n- Increments `totSeatsInUse`, `totRequestsExecuting`, emits metrics.\n- Calls `boundNextDispatchLocked` as an anti-windup guard (see \u00a74.4).\n\n### 3.4 Waiting: `request.wait()`\n\n`queueset.go:399`\n\nThe caller's goroutine blocks in `req.Finish(executeFunc)`:\n\n```go\nfunc (req *request) Finish(execFn func()) bool {\n    exec, idle := req.wait()     // blocks here\n    if !exec { return idle }\n    defer req.qs.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n    execFn()\n    return idle\n}\n```\n\n`wait()` calls `req.decision.Get()`, which blocks until either:\n- The dispatch loop sets the decision to `decisionExecute`, or\n- The context is cancelled/timed out, causing the promise to self-resolve to `decisionCancel`.\n\nOn context cancellation, `req.cancelWaitingLocked()` is invoked: the request is removed from the FIFO list via its `removeFromQueueLocked` closure (O(1)), counts are decremented, metrics updated (`AddRequestsInQueues(-1)`), and a `\"time-out\"` or `\"cancelled\"` rejection reason is emitted.\n\n### 3.5 Completion: `finishRequestLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:863`\n\nWhen `execFn()` returns, `finishRequestLocked` is called under lock:\n\n1. Records actual service duration: `actualDuration = now - req.startTime`.\n2. **Seat adjustment**: `queue.nextDispatchR -= InitialSeats \u00d7 (estimatedServiceDuration - actualDuration)`. If the request finished faster than estimated, the queue's virtual time cursor is moved back, effectively giving it a credit.\n3. Removes the request from `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n4. **Two-phase seat release**:\n   - **Initial seats** (`InitialSeats`): released immediately by decrementing `totSeatsInUse`.\n   - **Final seats** (`FinalSeats`, for `AdditionalLatency` duration): if `AdditionalLatency > 0`, schedules `clock.EventAfterDuration(releaseSeatsLocked, additionalLatency)`. The deferred callback decrements seats and calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` again to unblock any waiting requests.\n5. Calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` to use the freed capacity immediately.\n\n---\n\n## 4. The Fairness Algorithm: Virtual Time and Seats\n\n### 4.1 Seat-Seconds: The Unit of Work\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/seat_seconds.go`\n\n`SeatSeconds` is a `uint64` fixed-point type with scale `1e8`:\n\n```go\nconst ssScale = 1e8\nfunc SeatsTimesDuration(seats float64, duration time.Duration) SeatSeconds {\n    return SeatSeconds(int64(math.Round(\n        seats * float64(duration/time.Nanosecond) / (1e9 / ssScale))))\n}\n```\n\nThe scale provides sub-microsecond precision without floating-point accumulation errors.\n\nA request's total work is:\n\n```\ntotalWork = InitialSeats \u00d7 estimatedServiceDuration\n          + FinalSeats \u00d7 AdditionalLatency\n```\n\n`estimatedServiceDuration` (default 3 ms, `queueset.go:94`) is the QueueSet-global estimate used at enqueue time; actual duration adjusts `nextDispatchR` after the fact.\n\n### 4.2 Virtual Time Rate: `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:526`\n\n```\nrate = min(totalSeatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n\nwhere:\n  totalSeatsRequested = \u03a3_queue (seatsInUse + maxSeatsWaiting)\n  activeQueues        = count of queues with any activity\n```\n\nThis rate governs how fast `currentR` advances per real second. The intuition:\n\n- When demand exceeds capacity (`totalSeatsRequested \u2265 ConcurrencyLimit`), `rate = ConcurrencyLimit / activeQueues`. Each active queue receives an equal share of the virtual clock advancement \u2014 fair allocation.\n- When demand is below capacity, `rate = totalSeatsRequested / activeQueues`. The virtual clock slows so that idle queues do not accumulate unredeemed credit.\n\n### 4.3 Virtual Time Synchronisation: `syncTimeLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:465`\n\n```go\nincrR = SeatsTimesDuration(rate, realTimeDelta)\ncurrentR += incrR\n```\n\nCalled at every lock acquisition via `lockAndSyncTime`. This means `currentR` is not a background ticker \u2014 it advances lazily, only when a request arrives, departs, or the config changes.\n\n### 4.4 Anti-Windup: `boundNextDispatchLocked`\n\n`queueset.go:952`\n\nA queue that receives no traffic for a long period would accumulate a `nextDispatchR` far below `currentR`. If traffic then resumed, that queue would appear to have massive credit and dominate dispatch for an extended burst. The anti-windup guard corrects this:\n\n```go\nif queue.nextDispatchR < oldestReq.arrivalR {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = oldestReq.arrivalR\n}\n```\n\nThe queue's virtual start time cannot precede the arrival time of its oldest waiting request. This is called immediately after a request is enqueued (`shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked`, line 622) and after each dispatch (`dispatchLocked`, line 744).\n\n### 4.5 Epoch Advancement: Overflow Prevention\n\n`queueset.go:489`\n\n`SeatSeconds` is a `uint64`. Unchecked, very long-running servers would overflow. When `currentR >= highR` (= 3/4 of `MaxSeatSeconds`):\n\n```go\nif qs.currentR >= highR {\n    qs.currentR -= rDecrement          // subtract MaxSeatSeconds/2\n    for _, queue := range qs.queues {\n        queue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n        // adjust all waiting requests' arrivalR\n    }\n}\n```\n\nAll virtual-time values are shifted down by `rDecrement` (= `MaxSeatSeconds/2`) atomically under the lock. This keeps the representation in a safe range without disrupting relative ordering. The `AddEpochAdvance` metric records when this occurs.\n\n### 4.6 Max-Min Fairness Behaviour\n\nThe combination of:\n1. WFQ selection (smallest virtual finish time wins),\n2. equal virtual time rate per active queue,\n3. anti-windup bounding,\n\nimplements **max-min fairness**: in steady state, all active flows sharing a priority level converge to equal throughput. A flow with lighter requests will dispatch them more frequently, but each request costs fewer seat-seconds, so the total resource consumption remains equal. A flow that is temporarily absent does not accumulate unbounded future credit.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Rejection Paths\n\n| Reason | Trigger | Where |\n|---|---|---|\n| `\"concurrency-limit\"` | No-queue path: `totSeatsInUse + seats > ConcurrencyLimit` | `dispatchSansQueueLocked`, `queueset.go:313` |\n| `\"queue-full\"` | `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND `queue.Length() >= QueueLengthLimit` | `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked`, `queueset.go:560` |\n| `\"time-out\"` | Context deadline exceeded while waiting | `cancelWaitingLocked`, called from promise auto-cancel |\n| `\"cancelled\"` | Context cancelled by caller | Same path as time-out |\n\nWhen a request is rejected, `StartRequest` returns `nil` for the `Request`. The APF filter translates this into an HTTP 429 response. Note that a single queue being full does not trigger rejection if `totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit`; the request can still be admitted if other queues have room and are below the length limit \u2014 but the hash fixes which queue a flow maps to, so a saturated queue for a specific hash *does* cause rejection for that flow.\n\n### 5.2 Seat Accounting Inconsistency Window\n\nBetween the time `InitialSeats` are released (end of `execFn`) and `FinalSeats` are released (after `AdditionalLatency`), the seats are not reflected in `totSeatsInUse` for the initial phase but the final-phase goroutine has not yet run. In this window, new requests may be dispatched that could not have been dispatched if final seats were still counted. This is intentional: the final phase represents lightweight cleanup (e.g., waiting for a response body flush) that does not require the same level of admission control as the main execution.\n\n### 5.3 Estimator Dependency\n\nThe work estimate `InitialSeats` and `FinalSeats` are provided by an external estimator injected at the controller level (`apf_controller.go:1069`). If the estimator systematically underestimates seats (e.g., for watch requests), the QueueSet dispatches more requests than the actual server can handle, leading to latency spikes rather than predictable queuing. If it overestimates, throughput is wasted. This is the main operational tuning surface.\n\n### 5.4 Single-Queue Lock Contention\n\nThe entire `queueSet` is protected by one `sync.Mutex`. Under high request rates, this lock becomes a bottleneck regardless of the number of queues. The dispatch loop in `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` runs entirely under the lock, making the critical section proportional to the number of simultaneous dispatchable requests. For typical configurations (128 queues, concurrency limit in the hundreds), this has not been observed as a bottleneck in practice, but it is a hard architectural ceiling.\n\n### 5.5 Queue Count vs. Isolation Tradeoff\n\nMore queues improve isolation (a bad actor can only occupy `handSize` of them) but increase memory and the cost of `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` (which scans all queues). `handSize` (shuffle-sharding hand size) is a separate parameter: larger hands improve load balancing at the cost of weaker isolation. The default configuration balances these for typical multi-tenant clusters.\n\n### 5.6 Draining Queues During Reconfiguration\n\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues` decreases, the excess queues are not destroyed. They remain in `qs.queues` and continue to drain in-progress requests. New requests are only hashed into the reduced deck via the updated `Dealer`. Draining queues are removed lazily in `removeEmptyQueue` when they become idle. This means a config change that shrinks queues temporarily increases memory usage and extends the scan in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 6.1 `QueueSetFactory` Interface\n\n`fairqueuing/interface.go:34`\n\nThe factory is the primary injection point. The default implementation is `queueset.NewQueueSetFactory`, but an alternative can be injected for testing or custom scheduling policies. Tests in `queueset_test.go` use a synthetic factory that wires in a fake clock and fake metrics, enabling deterministic replay.\n\n### 6.2 `promiseFactory` Function Type\n\n`queueset.go:88`\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n```\n\nInjected into `queueSet` at construction. In production this is `writeoncePromise.NewWriteOnce`; in tests it is a custom implementation that allows synchronised promise resolution. Swapping this factory enables testing of cancellation races without real goroutines.\n\n### 6.3 `QueueNoteFn` Callback\n\n`fairqueuing/interface.go:104`\n\n```go\ntype QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\n```\n\nPassed in by the APF filter per-request. Called with `true` when the request enters a queue and `false` when it leaves (either dispatched or cancelled). The filter uses this to start and stop the \"waiting in queue\" latency timer for metrics. This is a clean separation: the QueueSet does not know about HTTP-level metrics.\n\n### 6.4 `EventClock` Injection\n\n`fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`\n\nThe `EventClock` interface abstracts all time operations. Injecting a fake clock (as done in `queueset_test.go`) lets tests advance time to millisecond precision without sleeping, making the test suite fast and deterministic. Any operator wishing to instrument time (e.g., for debugging time-warping scenarios) can inject a wrapping clock.\n\n### 6.5 Metrics Injection via `RatioedGauge` and `RatioedGaugePair`\n\nBoth are passed in at factory construction time. The QueueSet only calls `Set`, `Add`, `SetDenominator` on these interfaces \u2014 it never imports Prometheus directly. This allows the implementation to be tested with in-memory gauge stubs and avoids Prometheus registration side effects in tests.\n\n### 6.6 `WorkEstimate` as a Per-Request Policy Hook\n\n`request/width.go:34`\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimate struct {\n    InitialSeats      uint64\n    FinalSeats        uint64\n    AdditionalLatency time.Duration\n}\n```\n\nThe estimator function (`workEstimator func() fcrequest.WorkEstimate`) is provided by the filter as a closure over the HTTP request. It can be extended by operator-specific logic to, for example, assign higher seat counts to bulk list operations or write requests, changing their effective weight in the fair-queuing algorithm without modifying the QueueSet itself.\n\n**Risk**: An estimator that returns inconsistent seat counts for the same request verb/resource can break max-min fairness guarantees. Overestimation wastes concurrency; underestimation allows excessive dispatch.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n**Admission cost**: `StartRequest` acquires the lock, runs `syncTimeLocked` (one time.Now() call, one multiplication), runs shuffle sharding (O(handSize) iterations over a pre-computed hand), and if dispatching, runs one O(numQueues) scan in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`. For a 128-queue set with hand size 8, this is approximately 130 pointer dereferences per request admission under the lock \u2014 negligible compared to the HTTP handling cost.\n\n**Dispatch throughput**: `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` runs until no request can be dispatched. Each iteration is O(numQueues). In burst scenarios where many requests unblock simultaneously, this can iterate up to `concurrencyLimit` times per `finishRequest` call, each costing O(numQueues). For typical limits (hundreds of concurrent requests, 128 queues), this is measured in microseconds.\n\n**Memory**: Each queue holds a doubly-linked list of `*request` nodes. Memory is bounded by `DesiredNumQueues \u00d7 QueueLengthLimit \u00d7 sizeof(request)`. With 128 queues and a length limit of 100, this is about 12,800 request objects per priority level, each approximately 200 bytes \u2014 roughly 2.5 MB per priority level.\n\n### 7.2 Reliability: Guaranteed Forward Progress\n\nThe dispatch algorithm has no livelock: if any queue has waiting requests and `totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit`, `dispatchLocked` will always find a request to dispatch. This follows from the WFQ selection: there will always be a queue with a finite `nextDispatchR + totalWork()`. The only way a request can remain waiting indefinitely is if `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` continuously \u2014 which means all concurrency is occupied and the system is at its designed maximum throughput.\n\nContext cancellation provides the escape hatch: a waiting request whose deadline passes is removed without holding up the queue or blocking the dispatch path.\n\n### 7.3 Reliability: Config Change Safety\n\nThe two-phase config change pattern (`BeginConfigChange` / `Complete`) ensures that:\n- Config validation happens before any state mutation.\n- The new config is applied under the lock along with a `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` call, so requests that become dispatchable under increased concurrency limits are immediately unblocked.\n- Requests in queues that are being removed continue to execute; no in-flight work is dropped.\n\nAn operator reducing `ConcurrencyLimit` during a traffic spike should expect an increase in queue depth and 429 responses until the executing set drains to the new limit.\n\n### 7.4 Maintainability: Lock Naming Conventions\n\n`queueset.go:74\u201384` documents a strict convention:\n\n- `Locked` suffix: caller must hold `qs.lock`.\n- `ToBoundLocked` suffix: caller must call `boundNextDispatchLocked` immediately after.\n- No suffix: does not require the lock, or acquires it internally.\n\nThis convention is enforced by code review, not the type system. Violations would cause data races detectable with `-race`. The test suite runs with the race detector enabled.\n\n### 7.5 Observability\n\nKey metric signals for diagnosing APF behaviour:\n\n| Metric | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_requests_in_queues_total` | Depth of each priority level's queues; high sustained values indicate the level is undersized. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_concurrency_in_use` | Ratio of in-use seats to `ConcurrencyDenominator`; approaching 1.0 means the level is saturated. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total` | Throughput per priority level and flow schema. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` | Rate and reason (`queue-full`, `concurrency-limit`, `time-out`). The reason distinguishes queueing pressure from execution pressure. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_r` | The virtual clock value; should advance smoothly. Stalls indicate no active queues. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_next_s_bounds` | Min/max of `nextDispatchR` across queues; large spread indicates one queue is far ahead of others, which can suppress fairness temporarily. |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advances_total` | Should be rare. Frequent advances could indicate unusually high request volume or very long service times. |\n\n### 7.6 Known Operational Pitfalls\n\n**Watch requests and seat starvation**: Watch requests typically have long `AdditionalLatency` and non-trivial `FinalSeats`. If many watch connections accumulate, their final-phase seats can approach `ConcurrencyLimit`, blocking all other dispatching until the event callbacks fire. The `FinalSeats` cap (`queueset.go:824`) mitigates the worst case but does not eliminate it.\n\n**Thundering herd on config change**: When `ConcurrencyLimit` increases (e.g., after scaling the apiserver or editing a `PriorityLevelConfiguration`), `setConfiguration` calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`, which can unblock a large number of waiting requests simultaneously. Each dispatched request will contend for apiserver resources at the same time. Operators increasing limits should do so gradually if the request backlog is deep.\n\n**Virtual clock stall under zero load**: When there are no active queues, `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked` returns 0 and `currentR` does not advance. This is correct \u2014 there is no work to account for \u2014 but metrics dashboards showing `current_r` may appear to stall unexpectedly during quiet periods.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File and Directory Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_controller.go           # APF controller: FlowSchema matching, request routing,\n\u2502                               #   config reconciliation. Calls QueueSet.StartRequest and\n\u2502                               #   QueueSet.BeginConfigChange/Complete.\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_filter.go               # HTTP filter: calls startRequest, then req.Finish(executeFunc).\n\u2502                               #   Owns the QueueNoteFn that drives waiting-latency metrics.\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 fairqueuing/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 interface.go            # Public interfaces: QueueSetFactory, QueueSetCompleter,\n\u2502   \u2502                           #   QueueSet, Request, QueueNoteFn, QueuingConfig,\n\u2502   \u2502                           #   DispatchingConfig. The contract between controller and impl.\n\u2502   \u2502\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 integrator.go           # Time-weighted integrator for seat-demand statistics (avg,\n\u2502   \u2502                           #   min, max, stddev). ## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries

### What Problem It Solves

The API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem enforces fair, priority-aware admission control for API server requests. Without it, a single misbehaving client or controller with many concurrent requests can monopolize the apiserver's in-flight capacity, starving other consumers. APF replaces the older max-inflight mechanism with a multi-level queuing system that:

- Separates requests into distinct *priority levels*, each with its own concurrency budget.
- Within a priority level, subdivides requests across many *flow queues* via shuffle sharding so that one hostile flow cannot saturate the level.
- Applies virtual-time fair queuing so that flows sharing a level converge toward equal bandwidth even when requests have heterogeneous resource costs (measured in *seats* and *seat-seconds*).

### Subsystem Boundaries

**Upstream boundary — the APF controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`): The controller holds the live `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects, matches each incoming 
... (truncated)
